  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_07a94069-6ecf-40dc-8496-19f47da79dbe'

  <span id="freeText12802208688807371488" style="display:none">  ✔Spell binding ✔Sexy ✔Romantic ✔Monster Romance ✔Vampire   <br /> <br /><i> “She gave me life again. She is the reason why I came to life and why I am breathing. Her blood calls out to me like a siren that I cannot ignore. Who is she, you ask? Why, she is My Beloved.” </i> <br /> <br />It was in English class that Wendy heard of a tale about the vampire, Vincent Gilmore, who was buried alive by the townspeople along with their silver. The only thing interesting about it was the silver, which Wendy sure could put to good use for her brother’s surgery. <br /> <br />Wendy was shocked to find that the tale was indeed true, for there, after digging his grave, she came face to face with his rotting corpse, and the mound of silver that she took home. <br /> <br />Unknowingly, Wendy set a series of events that would forever change her life. Her blood brought Vincent back to life, but it wasn’t her blood alone. They were destined to be together. <br /> <br />Because she was his Beloved.</span>

<div id="review_1188713450" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1188713450" />
    <a title="Joanna Choi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13404467-joanna-choi"><img alt="Joanna Choi" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1188713450?book_show_action=true">Feb 02, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Joanna Choi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Joanna Choi" href="/user/show/13404467-joanna-choi">Joanna Choi</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook " href="/book/show/23737159-my-beloved">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1188713450" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6281677203726890956">I don't like writing mean reviews, but this was a really stupid book. If I had to take a guess based on this book, I would say that the author is a middle school student. Why? Because that's how the characters and the plot read. I'm always amazed that authors don't realize that characters are what really drive a story. Plots are rarely ever original, especially when you're dealing with tropes such as vampires falling in love with a teenager. This means that the characters need to be real, their </span>
  <span id="freeText6281677203726890956" style="display:none">I don't like writing mean reviews, but this was a really stupid book. If I had to take a guess based on this book, I would say that the author is a middle school student. Why? Because that's how the characters and the plot read. I'm always amazed that authors don't realize that characters are what really drive a story. Plots are rarely ever original, especially when you're dealing with tropes such as vampires falling in love with a teenager. This means that the characters need to be real, their interactions needs to be grounded in reality as to how people really behave, and you have to bring a healthy does of reality into the fantasy world that is being written. Here, none of that is present.<br /><br />Wendy is a high school student who has issues. Of course she does because these days every heroine has issues. Wendy's are serious because her brother is in the hospital dying. So, maybe that explains her parents' distraction. Still, the author mentions how the family is close, especially Wendy and her father, and yet the parents don't really notice anything being off with Wendy's behavior. Wendy suddenly has a new friend, one that she is so close to that she's spending the night, and the parents don't think it's weird that they've never even heard of her before. But aside from their parental failures, Wendy is just too much of an immature high school student for me to feel any sympathy or connection to her. Sure, she's young, but she needs to be mature beyond her age to explain why a 400-year-old vampire would be attracted to her--other than physically. Vincent is no better because he's a walking tantrum, although the author tries to explain that. Only, she doesn't succeed in excusing his behavior.<br /><br />But aside from the character failings, this book needs an editor. The author switches from past to present tense where it should not be done. It's as though the author was taught by teachers to use the present tense and so attempts to do that. Only, you don't really do that in books. So, the bad grammar, the bad characters, and boring plot all combined for a real time waster for me.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6281677203726890956" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText4204407152167438410" style="display:none">*Deep breath*<br />This. Book. Is. <br />Amazing. <br />This was the first book I ever read on wattpad. <span id="freeTextContainer3839192516236433712">The first time I read this book was on Wattpad and I can honestly say I loved it. I have read it over a million times since then (this is me being metaphorical) and its power to hold me captivated does not diminish. It has a brilliant plot and lovable characters that one can totally relate to. The thing that stopped me from giving it 5 stars is that I found it too surreal as a story. Everything happened so fast and there were so many things happening at the same time that I found that for me the</span>
  <span id="freeText3839192516236433712" style="display:none">The first time I read this book was on Wattpad and I can honestly say I loved it. I have read it over a million times since then (this is me being metaphorical) and its power to hold me captivated does not diminish. It has a brilliant plot and lovable characters that one can totally relate to. The thing that stopped me from giving it 5 stars is that I found it too surreal as a story. Everything happened so fast and there were so many things happening at the same time that I found that for me there was not enough description - and by description I mean there were not enough words written to convey all that I feel the characters wanted to convey. I have nothing against short novels. Nonetheless, the length of the novel as compared to the depth of the plot and the amount of things occurring, I found, is too short. But other than that - LOVE.</span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40833509-aly?shelf=includes-vampires">includes-vampires</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40833509-aly?shelf=age-new-adult">age-new-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40833509-aly?shelf=includes-smut">includes-smut</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2326686850" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11569400674387827281">4/5 stars<br/><br/>I really enjoyed this book. I couldn't put it down as soon as I started reading. I was a bit skeptical the first few chapters as i was unsure on how the author would go about it, but I ended up enjoying the ride. It was a different take on vampire romance, and I felt it was a solid book. Although the conflict near the 3 quarter mark of the book was lackluster, I found the rest of it to be really enjoyable and fun. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer11355872929426344858"><strong>Horrible writing</strong><br/><br/>The premise was very good and that is the only reason I made it to 26% before quitting in frustration. The writing was very stunted. Think high school creative writing class. I wanted to finish but it was that bad. If the author were to get an editor or a ghost writer... I would try again. A little disappointing but thank goodness for kindle unlimited. </span>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer17427519286524061781">Part of Kindle Unlimited. HEA - Not your typical vampire book. She still in high school - she is not popular - she is his Beloved. He is a Vampire who was blamed for something he didn't do - he is trapped for hundreds of years - he can only be rescued by his Beloved. The twists keep on coming....major one near the end - Oh and there is not 1 but 2 wicked witches. 4 1/2 star read from me.</span>

          </span>

<li class='cover' id='bookCover_33821992'>
<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/33821992-the-practice-boyfriend"><img alt="The Practice Boyfriend (Boyfriend #1)" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/books/1483923819l/33821992._SX98_.jpg" />

<script type="text/javascript" charset="utf-8">
//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('/ham2oiAUzKIgpUHe2yxpRqnBN2WwWE7x+d/xFjTHVIHNM4R1d7Cvk5nj2s1rrQuUit9E8p5Y106my30hFBTWw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('VxocmdBmU4yiixDh6rBybAx1GlnBpH69kJoBQ13XBcmuOHRSjTjCAGRuCo2kcnfnRPljl50cfNtt5lNzgVRLwA==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

          $$('div.prototip').each(function(i){i.setStyle({zIndex: $('box').getStyle('z-index')})});
        } else {
          $$('div.prototip').each(function(i){i.setStyle({zIndex: 6000})});
        }
      });

      newTip['wrapper'].addClassName('prototipAllowOverflow');

        $('bookCover_15758438').observe('prototip:shown', function () {
          $$('div.prototip').each(function (e) {
            if ($('bookCover_15758438').hasClassName('ignored')) {
              e.setStyle({'display': 'none'});
              return;
            }
            e.setStyle({'overflow': 'visible'});
          });
        });
      $('bookCover_15758438').observe('prototip:hidden', function () {
        $$('span.elementTwo').each(function (e) {
          if (e.getStyle('display') !== 'none') {
            var lessLink = e.next();
            swapContent(lessLink);
          }
        });
      });

//]]>
</script>

</li>
</ul>
